  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5871876783758440532"><b>See the world of <i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> anew through the eyes of Christian Grey.</b><br/><b><br/>In Christian's own words, and through his thoughts, reflections, and dreams, E L James offers a fresh perspective on the love story that has enthralled millions of readers around the world.</b><br/><br/>Christian Grey exercises control in all things; his world is neat, disciplined, and utterly empty—until the </span>
  <span id="freeText5871876783758440532" style="display:none"><b>See the world of <i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> anew through the eyes of Christian Grey.</b><br /><b><br />In Christian's own words, and through his thoughts, reflections, and dreams, E L James offers a fresh perspective on the love story that has enthralled millions of readers around the world.</b><br /><br />Christian Grey exercises control in all things; his world is neat, disciplined, and utterly empty—until the day that Anastasia Steele falls into his office, in a tangle of shapely limbs and tumbling brown hair. He tries to forget her, but instead is swept up in a storm of emotion he cannot comprehend and cannot resist. Unlike any woman he has known before, shy, unworldly Ana seems to see right through him—past the business prodigy and the penthouse lifestyle to Christian’s cold, wounded heart.  <br /><br />Will being with Ana dispel the horrors of his childhood that haunt Christian every night? Or will his dark sexual desires, his compulsion to control, and the self-loathing that fills his soul drive this girl away and destroy the fragile hope she offers him?<br /><br /><b>This book is intended for mature audiences.</b></span>

      </div>

<div id="review_1310432499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1310432499" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406624675p2/31339793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1310432499?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

          marked it as did-not-finish


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25643846-grey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=dont-judge-me">dont-judge-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=baby-is-fuckin-overrated">baby-is-fuckin-overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=i-cannot-even-comprehend">i-cannot-even-comprehend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1310432499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18303272926302375328"><b>DNF @ 5% aka Chap 3 </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402653364ra/9967136.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My perception of Christian Grey is officially ruined and it seems that I've been living a lie. <br/><br/>I tried, I really did. But Grey's inner monologue was written terribly which butchered his character and had me eye-rolling at the absurdity of the way he talks in his head (the repetitive "baby" term nearly had me belting out a Bieber song). He sounded like a juvenile <s>kid</s> guy with these strange italic monologues and the inappropriate usage of exclamation marks. Just an example from</span>
  <span id="freeText18303272926302375328" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 5% aka Chap 3 </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402653364ra/9967136.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My perception of Christian Grey is officially ruined and it seems that I've been living a lie. <br><br>I tried, I really did. But Grey's inner monologue was written terribly which butchered his character and had me eye-rolling at the absurdity of the way he talks in his head (the repetitive "baby" term nearly had me belting out a Bieber song). He sounded like a juvenile <s>kid</s> guy with these strange italic monologues and the inappropriate usage of exclamation marks. Just an example from the a few pages itself:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>She peeks up at me and bites down on her full bottom lip.<br><i>Fuck! How did I not notice how inviting that mouth is?</i><br>"S-Sorry. I'm not used to this."<br><i>I can tell, baby, but right now I don't give a damn because I can't take my eyes off your mouth.</i><br>"Take all the time you need, Miss Steele." I need another moment to marshal my wayward thoughts.<br><i>Grey...stop this, now.</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And another:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><i>Yes!</i> She is affected by me. The knowledge is immensely pleasing. Strolling over to the elevator, I press the call button while she stands fidgeting beside me.<br><i>Oh, I could stop your fidgeting, baby.</i> <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And another:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>Absentmindedly, she wipes a crumb from the corner of her lips and into her mouth and sucks on her finger. My cock twitches in response.<br><i>What am I, fourteen?</i><br>My body's reaction is irritating. Maybe this will stop if I fetter, fuck and flog her...and not necessarily in that order.<br><i>Yeah. That's what I need.</i> <br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And it just continues in a never ending loop of alternating between 'italics' monologues and 'normal' monologues (what even???!). I'm sorry EL James but this trilogy was much better off without this book. By 2 chapters alone, it has obliterated all the supposingly controlling, confident and dominant appeal for the Christian Grey that I've come to known. Now he sounds like an annoying pompous piece of a man with the most irritating inner monologue that sounds like a clingy woman or equivalent to a 5-year old kid. <br><br>It's completely unappealing and honestly, I can't even take his POV/this read seriously at all. It feels like a really bad horrible joke of a read. I don't want to sound insensitive but frankly, the writing was so poorly done that it has been reduced to at an amateur level. So I'm calling it quits to preserve my sanity. <br><br>P/S: Flipped to the last page and found out that this book only covers the first book in the trilogy. <br><br>P/P/S: This book is almost 500+ pages long. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18303272926302375328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11399318418426074041">Evidently this is intended as an homage to <i>Midnight Sun</i>, which given the roots of the Fifty Shades series is entirely appropriate and thematic. What I don't understand is why E.L.   <span id="freeText11399318418426074041" style="display:none">Evidently this is intended as an homage to <i>Midnight Sun</i>, which given the roots of the Fifty Shades series is entirely appropriate and thematic. What I don't understand is why E.L. James didn't arrange for a crazed fan to hack into her computer, steal the draft and leak it over the web, causing her to abandon the project in disgust when it was still in an incomplete form. What's <i>wrong</i> with her? Doesn't she <i>care</i>?<br />________________________________<br /><br />If you can't beat them, join them. No more carping and criticizing: clearly there is nothing much to it, and I have decided to become a world-famous erotic novelist as well. Here, rescued from its obscure position as message #43 in the comment thread, is the first page of my new bestseller, which I have provisionally entitled <i>My Grey Life</i>. Amazon will soon be accepting pre-orders.<blockquote>After a tempestuous night with an A-list movie star I probably should not identify, I rise early; my companion, exhausted by our naughty games, is still asleep, and I decide to let her get some well-earned rest. I do my usual workout at my fully-equipped private gym - those six-pack abs don't maintain themselves, my trainer always reminds me! - and then retire to the study where I plan to spend half an hour improving my mind. But I have only read a couple of pages from my signed first edition of Weyl's <i>Quantenmechanik und Gruppentheorie</i> when the door opens, and the housekeeper, a former Miss Honduras, arrives carrying a breakfast tray. As she smiles and leans over to put it on my Louis XIV escritoire, I ask my cock what he thinks of the bountiful assets she is so generously displaying. Imagine my consternation when I receive no answer. The little bastard has escaped again! He evidently made off while I was trying to decipher Weyl's rather terse explanation of spherical harmonics. It is the second time this week.<br /><br />My housekeeper notices my expression and asks me what's wrong; I shamefacedly confess my predicament, and together we search the room. We eventually run the miscreant to ground, hiding behind a massive armoire. Conchita, who seems to know what she is doing, goes down on her hands and knees and manages to coax him out, using a saucer of milk and an old copy of <i>Hustler</i>. I tuck him back into my underpants and resolve to double her salary with immediate effect. <br /><br />As you see, it's not as simple as you might think being a hunky billionaire with a sentient penis. But I relish the challenge and wouldn't have it any other way.</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6099142723612590364"><b>4 stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/f6c94767-373c-434f-b3b8-607ea3ffac98_zpsfprwupqy.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435570202i/15360472.jpg' alt=' photo f6c94767-373c-434f-b3b8-607ea3ffac98_zpsfprwupqy.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> is a series I will always hold near and dear to my heart. I’ve been an avid reader most of my life, but Fifty was the book that jump started my reading. It got me to start reading more romance, and with that, I joined groups on goodreads and found so many indie books I may have never discovered and made many friends I’m sure I would have never crossed paths with otherwise. I’ll keep this review fairly short, most people have read Fifty Shades so there is no need </span>
  <span id="freeText6099142723612590364" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/f6c94767-373c-434f-b3b8-607ea3ffac98_zpsfprwupqy.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435570202i/15360472.jpg" alt=" photo f6c94767-373c-434f-b3b8-607ea3ffac98_zpsfprwupqy.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> is a series I will always hold near and dear to my heart. I’ve been an avid reader most of my life, but Fifty was the book that jump started my reading. It got me to start reading more romance, and with that, I joined groups on goodreads and found so many indie books I may have never discovered and made many friends I’m sure I would have never crossed paths with otherwise. I’ll keep this review fairly short, most people have read Fifty Shades so there is no need to rehash that story. It’s a book you either love or hate- there doesn’t seem to be much in-between. I happen to love it. <br><br><i>Grey</i> is a retelling of the first Fifty book from Christian’s perspective. If you’re looking for an epic new story or all kinds of new material, you’ll be disappointed. Besides some extra looks into Christian’s past, there isn’t much new. I knew this going in and I was okay with it. I still enjoyed this one. I think the fact that I listened to it over a week or two opposed to reading it helped tremendously. The narration was FANTASTIC. Zachary Webber voiced Christian perfectly. If she brings the rest of the books out from Christian’s pov I will most definitely be listening to them on audio! <br><br><u>I would recommend this book to:</u><br>~Fans of the <i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> trilogy<br>~People who don’t mind retelling of the same story from a different perspective. <br><br>If you are neither of the above, this probably won’t be the book for you. But if you ARE both of the above I recommend you give this a go and highly recommend picking up the audio! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4773260774937495201">I actually downloaded this from the library as a potential back-up plan to get me out of jury duty. Turns out it wasn't necessary because Friday I received word the case had settled and my super qualified and totally not-judgey services wouldn't be necessary after all.   <span id="freeText4773260774937495201" style="display:none">I actually downloaded this from the library as a potential back-up plan to get me out of jury duty. Turns out it wasn't necessary because Friday I received word the case had settled and my super qualified and totally not-judgey services wouldn't be necessary after all. Buuuuuuuuuuuut I figure you can't make bad decisions all year unless you start on January 1 so I decided to read this today.<br><br>My reaction upon the announcement of yet another Stephanie Meyer rip-off and a "Grey" story rather than a "Rising Sun" release left me with a pretty strong reaction . . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433179573ra/15059643.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Surely this can't be serious . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433179573ra/15059644.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But now that I'm finished I have to say this was way better than the original. Having the book written from Christian's perspective definitely made him seem less creepy - even though his conversations with his . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483313270ra/21600356.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Rather than some sort of "inner goddess" were just as insufferable. <br><br>Obviously by my rating I still found it to be "just okay," but hell 2 Stars is better than the zero I'd like to give the first three in the series so I'm calling it a win. No need to troll me, I'm more than happy to admit Christian Grey is just not my cuppa (but as I said I appreciated the ownership of his fuck-up-edry way more this go 'round). I also just don't get off on the sexytimes contained in this series. They are soooooooo not sexy. I thought it was because I was a prude delving in to "Mommy Porn" when all the other horny geezers were reading this years ago, but now that I fly my freak flag prominently it's just the scenes themselves. For as "edgy" as they are supposed to be after reading the 17,469th copulation it pretty much became . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483313270ra/21600357.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oh and dare I forget that I wasn't aware of Christian being from England. E.L. James - your beta readers and/or editor failed a bit with the "have a lie in" and other very British phrasings that weren't switched around for us 'Muricans. Since you still sold eleventy trillion copies it seems I may have been the only one to catch that faux pas.<br><br>If you're a fan of Grey, stay a fan and don't apologize to anyone. Reading is fundamental - whether you're reading young adult, prize winners, comic books or smut. As Martha would say . . . .<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483313270ra/21600358.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4773260774937495201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession">Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1295752546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer78164263760764800"><b>5 Deeper Grey Stars</b><br/><br/>First read September 2015<br/>reread June 2017<br/><br/><b> Who love the fuck outta this book?</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/tumblr_mt7z4u0SEy1rqfhi2o1_500_zpsuqwxzinc.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442902007ra/16291890.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mt7z4u0SEy1rqfhi2o1_500_zpsuqwxzinc.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I loved the first book in this series, Fifty Shades of Grey , but I loved this one more. OMG I really didn't think I would like this book more . I mean I knew going into this, that I would most likely like it. I liked the first book and this is just the first book in Christian pov. I knew I would get a little more info about what was going on in Mr. Grey's fucked up mind, but the same story. I love</span>
  <span id="freeText78164263760764800" style="display:none"><b>5 Deeper Grey Stars</b><br><br>First read September 2015<br>reread June 2017<br><br><b> Who love the fuck outta this book?</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/tumblr_mt7z4u0SEy1rqfhi2o1_500_zpsuqwxzinc.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442902007ra/16291890.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mt7z4u0SEy1rqfhi2o1_500_zpsuqwxzinc.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved the first book in this series, Fifty Shades of Grey , but I loved this one more. OMG I really didn't think I would like this book more . I mean I knew going into this, that I would most likely like it. I liked the first book and this is just the first book in Christian pov. I knew I would get a little more info about what was going on in Mr. Grey's fucked up mind, but the same story. I loved seeing things from Christian's pov. It made me love him more. I know not everyone will agree with me and that is cool. We are all free thinking people and I love that, but when I wrote my review on Fifty Shades of Grey, I had some people message me or leave comments on my review that said all kinds of mean things. "I was weak minded." " I set the feminist movement back" " I was promoting domestic violence" ect ect. So please if you don't like this book or my review that is okay. Just don't send me hateful comments please. This review is just my silly little opinion and means nothing in the grand scheme of things!<br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/11282880_zpsqnpfbkng.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442902007ra/16291891.gif" alt=" photo 11282880_zpsqnpfbkng.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That being said, I loved seeing Christian fall in love. Seeing his thought's on Ana. It made me hate Elena more, which quite frankly is amazing because I hated that bitch so much already. My favorite part was the ending when their relationship is falling apart. This book gave me what I wanted that the first one didn't, which was to see what was going though Christian's mind when he realized he had taken it to far with Ana and what he did after she left him. I think getting to see Ana the way Christian seen her was also great because it not only made Ana more Personable, but it made Christian seem more real. I really enjoyed this book and I am sure most Fifty shades fans will. Grey made me miss the series so much I am going to reread book 2&amp;3. I really hope E.L. James makes books 2&amp;3 in Christian's pov . Hey a girl can dream!<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsession.blogspot.com/2015/09/grey.html">http://jessicasoverthetopbookobsessio...</a></span>

<div id="review_1295978496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1295978496" />
    <a title="Catarina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11538033-catarina"><img alt="Catarina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514808293p2/11538033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1295978496?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catarina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catarina" href="/user/show/11538033-catarina">Catarina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11538033-catarina?shelf=is-getting-hot-in-here">is-getting-hot-in-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11538033-catarina?shelf=filthy-billionaires">filthy-billionaires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1295978496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer955941968383328563"><b>2,5 Underwhelmed Stars. </b>	<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434757689ra/15259525.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>50 Shades of Grey, despite not being my favorite book series, caused a sensation, caught my attention and a few years ago, the curiosity to see if other people thought like me was what brought me to Goodreads. By that alone these books will always have a place in my heart. But this one… just left me underwhelmed. And mad, considering I’ve paid 4£ for it and could have bought a few books with that money. <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434757689ra/15259526.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’m not speaking about the story itself because being a male POV I </span>
  <span id="freeText955941968383328563" style="display:none"><b>2,5 Underwhelmed Stars. </b>	<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434757689ra/15259525.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>50 Shades of Grey, despite not being my favorite book series, caused a sensation, caught my attention and a few years ago, the curiosity to see if other people thought like me was what brought me to Goodreads. By that alone these books will always have a place in my heart. But this one… just left me underwhelmed. And mad, considering I’ve paid 4£ for it and could have bought a few books with that money. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434757689ra/15259526.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m not speaking about the story itself because being a male POV I knew exactly what was coming (and to be honest I did skim a bit). But let me tell you that when I read the books, even with the crazy amount of his issues, I always thought of Christian as sexy, confident and powerful. If you think of him the same way, don’t read this. He questions himself so much that you will start to think that he’s a pussy. E. L. James managed to turn the powerful mogul into a confused kitten. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425220212ra/13863459.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m not even going to talk about the atrocious writing because, again, I was counting on it. But if you’re going to write a book with more than 500 pages of a Male POV I expect you to cover at least the most important moments of the trilogy and add a new and nice epilogue. But, guess what? NOOO! Just the first f*cking book and the exact same story. Not even a 50 word new epilogue. If you’re going to milk the cow the most you can, at least learn to sell good milk!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434757689ra/15259527.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Super-hiper-mega fans of the series, will probably love this book and eat it alive. But if for you was just “meh”, I don’t advise you to buy it (at least while it doesn’t have a sale) because you will end up really mad with you and with the fact that your credit card actually let you buy this. For me it, despite not being awful, it was a big block of “meh”. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396883845ra/9198277.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Ps. But I did pay for this book and I did help the cow-milking business... so maybe I'm the dumb in all this. Damn.) </span>

<div id="review_1357395976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1357395976" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357395976?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25643846-grey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=smut">smut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=bat-shit-crazy">bat-shit-crazy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357395976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15274339038065899895"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/11/review-grey-by-e-l-james.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>SO. Right off the bat, I think we need to get this out of the way: YES. I read the FIFTY SHADES trilogy, and, YES, I liked it.<br/><br/>Guess what?<br/><br/>I liked TWILIGHT, too.<br/><br/>And THE HUNGER GAMES, and I bloodydamn love HARRY POTTER.<br/><br/>If you think that means I have crap taste in books, then good riddance.<br/><br/>If you think that means I love ALL the hyped-up books, you don't know me, so who cares what you think?<br/><br/>I read what I want and heaven help anyone who tries to make me feel bad about it.<br/><br/>*steps</span>
  <span id="freeText15274339038065899895" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/11/review-grey-by-e-l-james.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>SO. Right off the bat, I think we need to get this out of the way: YES. I read the FIFTY SHADES trilogy, and, YES, I liked it.<br><br>Guess what?<br><br>I liked TWILIGHT, too.<br><br>And THE HUNGER GAMES, and I bloodydamn love HARRY POTTER.<br><br>If you think that means I have crap taste in books, then good riddance.<br><br>If you think that means I love ALL the hyped-up books, you don't know me, so who cares what you think?<br><br>I read what I want and heaven help anyone who tries to make me feel bad about it.<br><br>*steps down from soapbox*<br><br>Honestly, I'm not terribly worried about that in Rabid Reads space, b/c lovers of speculative fiction tend to be a less judgmental crowd.<br><br>But when the top dozen Goodreads reviews are all, "Hell NO, we won't read this crap, and we'll be (not so) silently judging anyone who <i>does</i>," well . . . it makes me a little bit defensive.<br><br>That being said, I didn't love GREY, which is basically FIFTY SHADES OF GREY verbatim, but from Christian's perspective. I liked it well enough, and it definitely had me jonesing to reread the trilogy, but Christian direct from the source is a bit too much for me.<br><br>I need filtered Christian.<br><br>You know why?<br><br>B/c just like all the accusations that James knows not-one-thing about the BDSM community, guess what?<br><br>NEITHER DO I.<br><br>There's a reason these books appeal to the WASP community at large: we are the opposite of hardcore.<br><br>We enjoy a FICTIONALIZED account of BDSM that ultimately concludes with a hot bazillionaire not being nearly as hard a case as he thought he was. #sorrynotsorry<br><br>A real, deep-in-the-lifestyle Dominant would scare the hell out of me. Not b/c there's anything wrong with it, but b/c it's so radically outside my own personal purview.<br><br>Clearly, I am not alone in this.<br><br>E.L. James capitalized on that, and I say good for her.<br><br>So ultimately, I don't regret reading GREY, and if you also loved the FIFTY SHADES trilogy and think you're made of sterner stuff than I am, then I say go for it. BUT. If Christian-filtered-through-Ana was about as much as you could take, then I'd skip it. It's one thing to ogle him from a distance, but quite another to be inside his fifty-shades-of-fucked-up head. Recommended with qualifications.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15274339038065899895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25644993-grey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14302918-patty-wrapped-up-in-reading-book-blog?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1295688836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15184592847158897553"><b>*****4.5</b> <i>
  <b>"I WANT MORE"</b>
</i> <b>STARS*****</b><br/>{BR with Mel, Sharon, Tiff, Kelli, Jen, and Tera}<br/><br/><br/><b>I've come alive since I've known her. These last few weeks have been the most exciting, the most unpredictable, the most fascinating in my life. I've been enticed from my monochrome world into one rich with color - and yet she can't be what I need.</b><br/><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/aa70edda3c0012eb0ad66a620bdbc0a0_zps9k8clabu.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435542671i/15357960._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo aa70edda3c0012eb0ad66a620bdbc0a0_zps9k8clabu.jpg' width='365' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>I really loved this book!!<br/>It started off a little iffy for me but in the end, I freaking LOVED THIS!!!<br/><br/><br/><br/>Yes, there was plenty that seemed to be a regurgitation from</span>
  <span id="freeText15184592847158897553" style="display:none"><b>*****4.5</b> <i>
  <b>"I WANT MORE"</b>
</i> <b>STARS*****</b><br>{BR with Mel, Sharon, Tiff, Kelli, Jen, and Tera}<br><br><br><b>I've come alive since I've known her. These last few weeks have been the most exciting, the most unpredictable, the most fascinating in my life. I've been enticed from my monochrome world into one rich with color - and yet she can't be what I need.</b><br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/aa70edda3c0012eb0ad66a620bdbc0a0_zps9k8clabu.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435542671i/15357960._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo aa70edda3c0012eb0ad66a620bdbc0a0_zps9k8clabu.jpg" width="365" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>I really loved this book!!<br>It started off a little iffy for me but in the end, I freaking LOVED THIS!!!<br><br><br><br>Yes, there was plenty that seemed to be a regurgitation from the first book in the series, but we all should have expected this. It didn't bother me because I have such a deep love for the characters and this story. I mean, I've read the books <b>FOUR TIMES</b>!!! AND, I was one of those nutty fans who emailed E.L. James and BEGGED her to write the books over in Christian's POV. So this book was like an early Christmas gift to me. I loved that E.L. James dedicated it to all of us fans out there who loved the story so much and just couldn't get enough of it.<br><br><br><br><br>We do get a more in depth look into Christian's brutal early childhood with his birth mother and her pimp. Then his early years with the Greys' and there were times that I nearly cried for little Christian. He was so lost during his youth that he even contemplated suicide, but didn't because he knew just how much that would have devastated Grace.<br><br><br><br><br>The only issue I really had and it was mostly in the beginning of the book, was that Christian seemed to be the woman in the relationship. Always waiting for Ana to call, text, or email him. He couldn't even function during his every day life until he heard from her, and I don't remember him being this needy in the original books. However, once the sexy times starts, <b>HOLY HELL</b>, I remembered why I loved this man so much. The sex in Christian's POV is just as hot, if not <b>HOTTER</b>!!!<br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/giphy_zps5youstuz.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435201137ra/15316147.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zps5youstuz.gif" width="360" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>Also Christian's early history with Elena is revealed and what I did like was that after he starts seeing Ana, he doesn't seem to be all that affected or influenced by Elena. He spends a lot of time ignoring her texts and calls or brushing her off quickly when they do speak. <br><br><br><br>I found myself falling in love all over again with CG. Every time he would acknowledge that weird feeling in his chest whenever Ana would do or say something affectionate, I was swooning. I always thought of him as the alpha, who was in control, but really, it was Ana that had all the control. She was the one to break through his defenses and to make him question whether he may just be worthy of being loved.<br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/large%202_zpsftw29zhb.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435542671ra/15357961.gif" alt=" photo large 2_zpsftw29zhb.gif" width="365" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>For those of you who loved the "Fifty Shades" series, I highly recommend reading this book. BUT, go into it knowing that this is the same story just with some added insights into Christian's past and what his thoughts were during his month with Ana. The book doesn't end how "Fifty Shades of Grey" did. We get to experience Christian's dark days of depression while being apart from Ana, up until just before they meet to attend Jose's art gallery showing together. <br><br><br><br><br>I also heard that E.L. James will be writing <b>"Fifty Shade Darker"</b> in CG's POV too!!! I can't wait, and hopefully this means the third book will also be written in his POV!! <br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/tumblr_njo80tiJlZ1r7eta3o1_500_zpsw97blm2t.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435542671ra/15357962.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_njo80tiJlZ1r7eta3o1_500_zpsw97blm2t.gif" width="365" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15184592847158897553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7669472386882860814">Now, is E.L. James a clever writer or not!!!! Did we actually need this book??? Of course not!!   <span id="freeText7669472386882860814" style="display:none">Now, is E.L. James a clever writer or not!!!! Did we actually need this book??? Of course not!! GREY is exactly the same book as Fifty Shades of Grey and the earliest section of Fifty Shades Darker ..there's only one difference.........let me tell you more...<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1484686943i/21742117.jpg" alt=" photo f5acf994295e3bb9cef8bf18e4d123a2_zpsl0zq9u43.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1297116875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297116875" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505605297p2/13126896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297116875?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126896-michelle?shelf=01-signed">01-signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297116875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer424907881020252321">Fifty Shades of Grey was my introduction to romance. This was the first book I read in late 2012 in this particular genre. It is what convinced me to buy a kindle. It was what opened the door to a whole new world of stories. In a way this book changed my life. It brought a long list of friends that I hold near and dear to my heart and it has given me an outlet that I did not have before. Say what you will about this series, but there is no denying the impact it has had in the book world.<br/><br/>Some hat</span>
  <span id="freeText424907881020252321" style="display:none">Fifty Shades of Grey was my introduction to romance. This was the first book I read in late 2012 in this particular genre. It is what convinced me to buy a kindle. It was what opened the door to a whole new world of stories. In a way this book changed my life. It brought a long list of friends that I hold near and dear to my heart and it has given me an outlet that I did not have before. Say what you will about this series, but there is no denying the impact it has had in the book world.<br /><br />Some hate this series. Okay. But I can’t think of another book that has changed things quite like this. We have authors we love because this book gave them the courage to try. Nearly three years ago this series set me on a new path. This gave me a push to expand my boundaries and now I am getting a chance at doing something with my life that I love to do. <br /><br />When I finished Fifty Shades Freed, the POV chapters at the end made me want to devour the books all over again. And I did. I read them ten times in a row (remember, I hadn’t yet purchased a Kindle). So getting Grey... yeah that was like a dream come true. <br /><br />Grey covers the span of time from just before Ana walks into his office until he get gets her back at the start of FSD. The dialogue and email exchanges are the same – of course they are, they had to be. But what was different was getting in Christian’s head. It was watching him struggle with his desire for her, his need of punishment and ultimately his undoing. <br /><br />I loved this book. I wanted the rest of the trilogy from his POV immediately. I had to open up Darker just to get the resolution I needed to feel OK. And well that, that turned into me re-reading all of that book. So yeah, it might be a few years since this story graced my kindle, but reading Grey reminded me of all I loved about it to begin with.<br /><br />So if you were not a fan of FSOG, this is not your book. Reading it would be a waste and really only will accomplish giving you a platform to pronounce your hate of the story. Why waste the money, time and effort for just a bit of attention? This book is one written or fans of the series. And this fan would gladly read the rest of this series through Christian Grey’s eyes if Ms. James was so inclined to write it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="424907881020252321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1295711175" />
    <a title="Claire Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14026987-claire-robinson"><img alt="Claire Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431471072p2/14026987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15957347839620278063"><strong>Every Bit As Good As The First Time!</strong><br/><br/>I loved every minute of this book! Usually, I get bored with alternate POV "retellings" because there isn't enough new material to keep me interested. This is one of the few stories that, even without too much new information, holds my attention every time. What can I say, it's a fantastic story! It was nice to finally get inside Christian's head.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296541819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7467657314158837478"><b>★★★★ 4.25 For-the-shades-of-grey I didn't even know existed..★★★★</b><br/><br/>I consider myself to be a <b>
  <u>NEUTRAL READER</u>
</b> in this scenario,since<b> I DO NOT HATE or LOVE this series</b>..This review is just <u><b>MY</b> humble opinion.</u><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434808223i/15264949._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i><b>'Grey'</b> is the fourth book belonging to the much know FSoG series which released its first film adaptation around Valentines this year.<br/><b>'GREY' is Book 1:'Fifty Shades Of Grey' written in Christian's POV..</b></i><br/><br/>I've never been a huge fan of the series from the beginning.But even though I never loved it</span>
  <span id="freeText7467657314158837478" style="display:none"><b>★★★★ 4.25 For-the-shades-of-grey I didn't even know existed..★★★★</b><br><br>I consider myself to be a <b>
  <u>NEUTRAL READER</u>
</b> in this scenario,since<b> I DO NOT HATE or LOVE this series</b>..This review is just <u><b>MY</b> humble opinion.</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434808223i/15264949._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i><b>'Grey'</b> is the fourth book belonging to the much know FSoG series which released its first film adaptation around Valentines this year.<br><b>'GREY' is Book 1:'Fifty Shades Of Grey' written in Christian's POV..</b></i><br><br>I've never been a huge fan of the series from the beginning.But even though I never loved it,I never hated it either.This book had DNF-ed with a lot of my besties here on GR which initially,I'll confess, had me worried.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434809140ra/15265062.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But like I said,I never had any specific expectations from the read and I only picked it up out of pure curiosity..<br><br>And well,I'm quite happy to say that I don't really regret my decision :)<br><br>I loved the fact that <b>Grey</b> was a far cry from Book one and had No <i>Inner goddesses</i> and sentence that ended with <i>'He looked like my popsicles' or 'chocolate caramels..'</i> <br><br>I think in this book, the author tried to re-shape her male character to give him more of a loving vibe to pacify readers who called Christian,putting it lightly,<b>'Overly Dominating'</b>at times.<br><br>A lot in this book surprised me,especially Christian inner monologue.It made him seem more sweeter and lovable compared to how he came across to Anna in book 1..<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Especially the glider scene,he seemed almost giddy with excitement about their air trip.. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434808223i/15264950.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It felt almost as if I was reading a more subtle version of the hero...I mean for god sake ! He worried over the fact that Anna didn't send an X(Kiss symbol) in one of her emails....Lol Come on ! Can you see Christian Grey worrying over something like THAT ? <br><br>Its too adorable to ignore !<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434809140ra/15265063.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u> About the cover..</u>
</b> *grimace* I didn't really like it...AT ALL.The whole 'eye' and 'filter' feature came cross as more <u>Supernatural</u> than an erotica or a contemproray read..Won't you say ? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434822469ra/15266943.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Final Verdict:</u>
</b>Over all it's a sweet read,I don't regret reading it.I'll admit they were some parts that bored me out,since this was book one's companion..and that out of the series I liked the other two better...<br><br><b>If a Book 5 comes out next,would I read it ?</b><br>Probably yes,I would..Like I said I liked the other two better in terms of story-line.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1311949768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1311949768" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1311949768?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25644993-grey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=favourites-2015">favourites-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=kinky">kinky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=mind-f">mind-f</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1311949768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14336523345947042338"><strong>Well no wonder Christian's 50 shades Mrs Robinson...</strong><br/><br/>I'm going to keep my review for Grey fairly short, after all we've been here before. I started this on Friday night with a glass of wine in my hand and a smirk on my face. Yes, it was a little more expensive than what I normally pay for an e-book and it was a story that I knew the ending to already. All I wanted was a few questions answered, so in essence I got exactly what I wanted...inside Christian's head.<br/><br/>The storyline was the same (surprise</span>
  <span id="freeText14336523345947042338" style="display:none"><strong>Well no wonder Christian's 50 shades Mrs Robinson...</strong><br /><br />I'm going to keep my review for Grey fairly short, after all we've been here before. I started this on Friday night with a glass of wine in my hand and a smirk on my face. Yes, it was a little more expensive than what I normally pay for an e-book and it was a story that I knew the ending to already. All I wanted was a few questions answered, so in essence I got exactly what I wanted...inside Christian's head.<br /><br />The storyline was the same (surprise, surprise) and the characters were the same (surprise, surprise), but it all felt a little different. Christian sees people in a way Anastasia doesn't. He is cynical, judgemental and abrupt. He pays people to do as he says and doesn't care what they think...until he meets and starts to care about Ana. The changes are slight as the story progresses, a thank you here and a thoughtful gesture there. We see this man with a stoic facade that shelters his vulnerable thoughts. At first he thinks it's just a matter of getting Ana to sign the contract, but she questions everything and some things he's not ready or willing to discuss. He's never felt this way before and doesn't handle the changes well. He can't comprehend why Ana can't just do as he says. He doesn't see it as him being bossy, he sees it as him trying to protect and look after her.<br /><br />The biggest draw for me in reading this story was finding out a little more about Mrs Robinson/Elena. I didn't think it would be possible but I hate her character even more now. Christian makes decisions based on what Mrs Robinson would think or say. Would Mrs Robinson approve of Ana? Should he introduce them? Should he drop everything to have dinner with Mrs Robinson? Would Mrs Robinson approve of the way he was handling things? If Christian did what Ana just did, what would Mrs Robinson's punishments be? It was all just a little creepy and as we know not resolved in the first book. Mrs Robinson still treats him as her submissive to some extent.<br /><br />Grey gave me some answers to questions I had and left me still wanting to know more. The sex scenes were hot, the thought processes interesting and Christian's protection of his submissive's past and present very evident. It wasn't a perfect read, but I still enjoyed it. I will definitely be going back for more.<br /><br />This review and more can be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://edgyreviews.com/">http://edgyreviews.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14336523345947042338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1295795660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1295795660" />
    <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts"><img alt="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591195447p2/16496589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1295795660?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts">Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1295795660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2071022459174195595"><b>I’ve seen various opinions regarding the imminent release of GREY. Some can’t wait, some don’t want and there are others who’re indifferent..... I wanted to get my thoughts out....<i> My reason to read...</i> </b><br/><br/>I fell in love with the exquisite love story of Anastasia Steele and Christian Grey, way before my kindle was an addiction or cleansing my book soul through reviewing was my obsession. When I completed my first read I felt my contentment juxtaposed against sheer desolation. I felt I was losing goo</span>
  <span id="freeText2071022459174195595" style="display:none"><b>I’ve seen various opinions regarding the imminent release of GREY. Some can’t wait, some don’t want and there are others who’re indifferent..... I wanted to get my thoughts out....<i> My reason to read...</i> </b><br><br>I fell in love with the exquisite love story of Anastasia Steele and Christian Grey, way before my kindle was an addiction or cleansing my book soul through reviewing was my obsession. When I completed my first read I felt my contentment juxtaposed against sheer desolation. I felt I was losing good friends, whatever would I read next that would ever compare? I wanted to keep all the feelings it gave me, cherish and preserve them. My second read evoked pretty much the same feelings and my quest for a plethora of epic 5 star love stories began and my reading world opened in the most exquisite manner. My reading quest led me to my alter ego Jxxx PinkLady, to many, many friends, special authors and most importantly, my reading besties who enhance my life every day. So you see this story is special in so many ways.<br><br><b>It’s a book I often feel like revisiting but with the hundreds of unread books now lining my kindle I don’t feel I have the time to devote to another re-read of the entire three book series. So this book, GREY gives me the perfect moment to stop, pause and reconnect with this story, however E.L. James chooses to present it to us. <i>It's imminent arrival in all honesty is giving me the book butterflies,</i> I'm super excited but in true British style I will endeavour to keep a lid on my exuberance. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/673049.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HYsqeIyKmIBYkhWHqIjMQ4WyLCgJc0MwJbwuiH3EttMnrUOqN9RR6P+5oeZffcacU+3L4Mf+zVd+wmg5sIdESQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2lWK2scWEuFBlOBEDSg4XBsjR2NsrTaTo5j66YylayPgc+MIfEjbiea/VCX63TKDzXygq6IguPT45rxYQeaZuQ==')})
  }

Grey is an erotic novel with aspects of romance tha<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7257424561791553704\" style=\"display:none\">SPECIAL DISCOUNT  (Regularly priced: \$3.99 \$2.99.)  Grey is the parallel narrative to the 50 Shades of Grey trilogy by E.L. James, from Christian Grey’s point of view rather than Anastacia Steele’s. Grey is an erotic novel with aspects of romance that delves into a topical display of the BDSM (bondage, discipline, sadism, masochism) lifestyle.  As a result of Grey only being told from Christian Grey’s point of view, the reader gets a strong sense of Grey’s past and his personal perspective via flashbacks, dreams, nightmares, and a constant internal monologue. The reader is told that Grey uses the “discipline” aspects of BDSM culture as a coping mechanism for the physical and psychological abuse he suffered as a child, between the ages of 3 and 4. Grey unintentionally shows stunted emotional growth and vents his frustrations with his subconscious self through “performative punishment” acts; he shows no emotional attachment to and of the women who agree to be his “submissives” until he meets and become infatuated with Anastacia Steele. Steele consumes his thoughts and fantasies before, during, and after their one-month, whirlwind relationship, and the novel ends when he commits to winning her back.  Grey as a novel reads at an elementary school level; outside of Grey’s dreams told from the point of view of toddler-aged Grey, the novel is simplistic at best, with instances of word misuse and extremely vague description. The character development is nominal; when presented with an adult with deep psychological scars, the author has given themselves the responsibility to develop them into a realistic character – many people have abuse in their pasts and can relate to this topic, therefore, when a writer establishes a character with substantial amounts of abuse, they need to give an equally substantial amount of consideration to the treatment of the character because the potential readers who don’t identify with the character could potentially carry over the same superficial treatment of a fictional character to a real person. That being said, James does not allow any growth for Grey as a character within the novel, except to move him towards “consideration” of growth rather than “actualization” of growth. She cuts Grey off at the proverbial knees, by keeping as an attractive, rich man with a kinky sex life and a shadowy background.   Would You Like To Know More? Download your copy today!
